  <h2>Properties</h2> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Properties Override"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Properties Override</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify where to get the overridden properties. Updates should not be made on portal.properties or on portal-bundle.properties, but in portal-ext.properties. </p> 
  <p>The default read order is: portal.properties, portal-bundle.properties, portal-ext.properties, and then portal-setup-wizard.properties. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    include-and-override=portal-bundle.properties
    include-and-override=${liferay.home}/portal-bundle.properties
    include-and-override=portal-ext.properties
    include-and-override=${liferay.home}/portal-ext.properties
    include-and-override=portal-setup-wizard.properties
    include-and-override=${liferay.home}/portal-setup-wizard.properties
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Each portal instance can have its own overriden property file following the convention portal-companyWebId.properties. To enable this feature, set the "company-id-properties" system property to true. </p> 
  <p>To enable: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     java ... -Dcompany-id-properties=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <p>The read order will now be: portal.properties, then portal-ext.properties, and then portal-liferay.com.properties. </p> 
  <p>Note that not all properties can have different values per company. This functionality is only available for legacy reasons. The preferred way to configure a portal instance is through the Control Panel. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    include-and-override=portal-${easyconf:companyId}.properties
    include-and-override=${liferay.home}/portal-${easyconf:companyId}.properties
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Additional property files can be used by setting the "external-properties" system property. </p> 
  <p>A common use case is to keep legacy property values when upgrading to newer versions of Liferay. To enable: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     java ... -Dexternal-properties=portal-legacy-5.1.properties
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <p>The read order will now be: portal.properties, then portal-ext.properties, and then portal-legacy-5.1.properties. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    include-and-override=${external-properties}
    include-and-override=${liferay.home}/${external-properties}
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Liferay Home"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Liferay Home</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the Liferay home directory. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    liferay.home=${resource.repositories.root}
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>This property is available for backwards compatibility. Please set the property "liferay.home" instead. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    resource.repositories.root=${default.liferay.home}
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Portal Context"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Portal Context</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the path of the portal servlet context. This is needed because javax.servlet.ServletContext did not have access to the context path until Java EE 5. </p> 
  <p>Set this property if you deploy the portal to another path besides root. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.ctx=/
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the application server's HTTP port. This value should be different from the value in the property "web.server.http.port". That property refers to the web server, this property refers to the application server. This property should only be set when the application server is sitting behind a web server like Apache. See LPS-17106 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.instance.http.port=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property if the application server is served behind a proxy and a prefix needs to be added to the portal servlet context path. This prefix will also be added to static resources served by layout templates, portlets, and themes. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.proxy.path=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="TCK"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>TCK</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable programmatic configuration to let the Portlet TCK obtain a URL for each test. This should never be set to true unless you are running the TCK tests. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    tck.url=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Schema"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Schema</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to automatically create tables and populate with default data if the database is empty. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    schema.run.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to to true to populate with the minimal amount of data. Set this to false to populate with a larger amount of sample data. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    schema.run.minimal=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Upgrade"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Upgrade</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class names that implement com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess. These classes will run on startup to upgrade older data to match with the latest version. </p> 
  <p>Escape the comma so that the property can be properly interpolated. For example, the property "upgrade.processes.6100" will not properly reference the property "upgrade.processes.default" unless the commas are escaped. See StartupHelper#getUpgradeProcessClassNames(String). </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.master=\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_0_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_1_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_1_2\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_1\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_2\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_3\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_1\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_2\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_3\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_5\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_6\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.5000=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5001=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5100=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5101=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5102=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5200=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5201=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5202=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.5203=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6000=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6001=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6002=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6003=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6004=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6005=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6006=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6100=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6101=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6110=${upgrade.processes.master}
    upgrade.processes.6120=${upgrade.processes.master}
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>This property is deprecated and only provided for backwards compatibility. If this property is specified with a list of classes, then the portal will use this list of upgrade processes without taking into account any of the other "upgrade.processes.*" property settings. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The following are upgrade processes for EE releases. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.5103=\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_1_5\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_1_6\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_1_7\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_1_7_to_5_2_7\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_7_to_6_0_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_1\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_2\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_3\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_5\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_6\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.5104=${upgrade.processes.5103}
    upgrade.processes.5105=${upgrade.processes.5103}
    upgrade.processes.5106=${upgrade.processes.5103}
    upgrade.processes.5107=${upgrade.processes.5103}
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>

        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_1_8_to_5_2_8\,\

        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_5\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_5_to_6_0_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_1\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_2\,\

        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>

</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.5206=\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_7\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_7_to_6_0_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_1\,\

        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.5207=${upgrade.processes.5206}
</pre>

  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.5208=\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_5_2_8_to_6_0_5\,\

        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_1

  <p></p>

  <p></p>

  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.6011=\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_12\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_0_12_to_6_1_0\,\
        com.liferay.portal.upgrade.UpgradeProcess_6_1_1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.processes.6012=${upgrade.processes.6011}
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to disable database transaction management during upgrades. This forces autocommit which will speed up the upgrade process. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    upgrade.database.transactions.disabled=true
</pre>

  <hr> 
  <a name="Verify"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Verify</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class name that implement com.liferay.portal.integrity.VerifyProcess. These classes will run on startup to verify and fix any integrity problems found in the database. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    verify.processes=com.liferay.portal.verify.VerifyProcessSuite
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the frequency for verifying the integrity of the database. </p> 
  <p>Constants in VerifyProcess: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     public static final int ALWAYS = -1;
     public static final int NEVER = 0;
     public static final int ONCE = 1;
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    verify.frequency=1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to disable database transaction management during verifies. This forces autocommit which will speed up the verify process. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    verify.database.transactions.disabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Convert"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Convert</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class names that implement com.liferay.portal.convert.ConvertProcess. These classes can be run from within the Admin portlet to convert older data to match a new configuration of the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    convert.processes=\
        com.liferay.portal.convert.ConvertDatabase,\
        com.liferay.portal.convert.ConvertDocumentLibrary,\
        com.liferay.portal.convert.ConvertDocumentLibraryExtraSettings,\
        com.liferay.portal.convert.ConvertPermissionAlgorithm,\
        com.liferay.portal.convert.ConvertPermissionTuner,\
        com.liferay.portal.convert.ConvertWikiCreole
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Auto Deploy"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Auto Deploy</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class names that implement com.liferay.portal.kernel.deploy.auto.AutoDeployListener. These classes are used to process the auto deployment of WARs. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.listeners=\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.ExtAutoDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.HookAutoDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.LayoutTemplateAutoDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.LiferayPackageAutoDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.PortletAutoDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.ThemeAutoDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.WebAutoDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.exploded.tomcat.HookExplodedTomcatListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.exploded.tomcat.LayoutTemplateExplodedTomcatListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.exploded.tomcat.PortletExplodedTomcatListener,\
       com.liferay.portal.license.deploy.auto.LicenseAutoDeployListener,com.liferay.portal.deploy.auto.exploded.tomcat.ThemeExplodedTomcatListener
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable auto deploy of layout templates, portlets, and themes. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the directory to scan for layout templates, portlets, and themes to auto deploy. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.deploy.dir=${liferay.home}/deploy
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the directory where auto deployed WARs are copied to. The application server or servlet container must know to listen on that directory. Different containers have different hot deploy paths. For example, Tomcat listens on "${catalina.base}/webapps" whereas JBoss listens on "${jboss.home.dir}/deploy". Set a blank directory to automatically use the application server specific directory. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.dest.dir=
    auto.deploy.default.dest.dir=../webapps
    auto.deploy.geronimo.dest.dir=${org.apache.geronimo.home.dir}/deploy
    auto.deploy.glassfish.dest.dir=${com.sun.aas.instanceRoot}/autodeploy
    auto.deploy.jboss.dest.dir=${jboss.home.dir}/standalone/deployments
    auto.deploy.jboss.dest.dir[5]=${jboss.server.home.dir}/deploy
    auto.deploy.jetty.dest.dir=${jetty.home}/webapps
    auto.deploy.jonas.dest.dir=${jonas.base}/deploy
    auto.deploy.resin.dest.dir=${resin.home}/webapps
    auto.deploy.tomcat.dest.dir=${catalina.base}/webapps
    auto.deploy.weblogic.dest.dir=${env.DOMAIN_HOME}/autodeploy
    auto.deploy.websphere.dest.dir=${env.USER_INSTALL_ROOT}/wsadmin-deploy
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the interval in milliseconds on how often to scan the directory for changes. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.interval=3000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the number of attempts to deploy a file before blacklisting it. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.blacklist.threshold=10
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if deployed WARs are unpacked. Set this to false if your application server has concurrency issues with deploying large WARs. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.unpack.war=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if plugins should automatically copy Commons Logging. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.copy.commons.logging=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if plugins should automatically copy Log4j. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.copy.log4j=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if you want the deployer to rename portlet.xml to portlet-custom.xml. This is only needed when deploying the portal on WebSphere 6.1.x with a version before 6.1.0.7 because WebSphere's portlet container will try to process a portlet at the same time that Liferay is trying to process a portlet. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.custom.portlet.xml=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to 1 if you are using JBoss' PrefixDeploymentSorter. This will append a 1 in front of your WAR name. For example, if you are deploying a portlet called test-portlet.war, it will deploy it to 1test-portlet.war. JBoss now knows to load this portlet after the other WARs have loaded. However, it will remove the 1 from the context path. </p> 
  <p>Modify /server/default/conf/jboss-service.xml. See org.jboss.deployment.scanner.PrefixDeploymentSorter. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.jboss.prefix=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the Glassfish settings to enable JSR 88 application deployment. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.glassfish.jee.deployment.enabled=false
    auto.deploy.glassfish.jee.dm.id=deployer:Sun:AppServer::localhost:4848
    auto.deploy.glassfish.jee.dm.user=admin
    auto.deploy.glassfish.jee.dm.passwd=adminadmin
    auto.deploy.glassfish.jee.df.classname=com.sun.enterprise.deployapi.SunDeploymentFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the path to Tomcat's configuration directory. This property is used to auto deploy exploded WARs. Tomcat context XML files found in the auto deploy directory will be copied to Tomcat's configuration directory. The context XML file must have a docBase attribute that points to a valid WAR directory. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.tomcat.conf.dir=../conf/Catalina/localhost
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the path to Tomcat's global class loader. This property is only used by Tomcat in a standalone environment. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.tomcat.lib.dir=../common/lib/ext
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>WebSphere 6 and 7 do not support the ability to hot deploy a WAR. The portal will attempt to use the wsadmin script to install a hot deployed plugin at runtime if this property is set. The wsadmin script uses this property to query the WebSphere application manager. Set this property to a blank value to disable this feature. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.websphere.wsadmin.app.manager.query=type=ApplicationManager,process=server1,*
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    auto.deploy.websphere.wsadmin.app.manager.query=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the suffix to be added to the plugin servlet context name in order to identify the WebSphere process it is deployed to. Leave it blank to use the plugin servlet context name only. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.websphere.wsadmin.app.name.suffix=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the properties file name to use when invoking the wsadmin command. Configure this property to change the the behavior of the wsadmin command, such as connection port or protocol. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auto.deploy.websphere.wsadmin.properties.file.name=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the URLs of libraries that might be needed to download during the auto deploy process. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    library.download.url.resin.jar=http://cdn.files.liferay.com/public/quercus/4.0.11/resin.jar
    library.download.url.script-10.jar=http://cdn.files.liferay.com/public/quercus/3.1.9/script-10.jar
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Hot Deploy"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Hot Deploy</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class names that implement com.liferay.portal.kernel.deploy.hot.HotDeployListener. These classes are used to process the deployment and undeployment of WARs at runtime. </p> 
  <p>The listeners are invoked in the order defined by this property. PluginPackageHotDeployListener must always be invoked first. SpringHotDeployListener must always be invoked before ServletContextListenerHotDeployListener. MessagingHotDeployListener must always be invoked last. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hot.deploy.listeners=\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.PluginPackageHotDeployListener,\
        \
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.SpringHotDeployListener,\
        \
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.ServletContextListenerHotDeployListener,\
        \
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.ExtHotDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.HookHotDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.LayoutTemplateHotDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.PortletHotDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.SocialHotDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.ThemeHotDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.ThemeLoaderHotDeployListener,\
        \
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.hot.MessagingHotDeployListener
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Hot Undeploy"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Hot Undeploy</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable undeploying plugins. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hot.undeploy.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the undeploy interval in milliseconds on how long to wait for the undeploy process to finish. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hot.undeploy.interval=0
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to undeploy a plugin before deploying a new version. This property will only be used if the property "hot.undeploy.enabled" is set to true. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hot.undeploy.on.redeploy=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Sandbox Deploy"></a>

  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    sandbox.deploy.listeners=\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.sandbox.PortletSandboxDeployListener,\
        com.liferay.portal.deploy.sandbox.ThemeSandboxDeployListener

  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    sandbox.deploy.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p>

  <p>Set the directory to scan for sand box style plugins. </p>

  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    sandbox.deploy.dir=${liferay.home}/sandbox
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the interval in milliseconds on how often to scan the directory for changes. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    sandbox.deploy.interval=3000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Plugin"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Plugin</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited supported plugin types. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    plugin.types=portlet,theme,layout-template,hook,web
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of Liferay plugin repositories separated by \n characters. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    plugin.repositories.trusted=http://plugins.liferay.com/official
    plugin.repositories.untrusted=http://plugins.liferay.com/community
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to false to avoid receiving on screen notifications when there is a new version of an installed plugin. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    plugin.notifications.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of plugin packages ids separated by \n characters. Administrators won't be notified when a new version of these plugins are available. The ids are of the form groupId/artifactId. You can also end the id with an asterisk to match any id that start with the previous character. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    plugin.notifications.packages.ignored=liferay/sample-jsp-portlet
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Portlet"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Portlet</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to set the default virtual path for all hot deployed portlets. See liferay-portlet-app_6_1_0.dtd and the virtual-path element for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.virtual.path=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to validate portlet.xml against the portlet schema. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.xml.validate=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Portlets that have configured liferay-portlet.xml with the element "add-default-resource" set to true will allow those portlets to be dynamically added to any page by any user. This is useful (and necessary) for some portlets that need to be dynamically added to a page, but it can also pose a security risk because it also allows any user to do it. </p> 
  <p>Set this property to true to add a security check around this behavior. If set to true, then portlets can only be dynamically added to a page if it contains a proper security token. This security token is automatically passed when using a portlet URL from one portlet to another portlet. </p> 
  <p>Modify the property "portlet.add.default.resource.check.whitelist" to whitelist certain portlets from this security check. </p> 
  <p>The security check utilizes the implementation set in the property "auth.token.impl". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.add.default.resource.check.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set a list of comma delimited list of portlet ids that will bypass the security check set in the property "portlet.add.default.resource.check.enabled". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.add.default.resource.check.whitelist=3,56_INSTANCE_0000,58,82,86,87,103,113,145,164,166,170,177
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited struts actions that will bypass the security check set in the property "portlet.add.default.resource.check.enabled". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.add.default.resource.check.whitelist.actions=\
        /journal/rss,\
        /language/view
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a regular expression to ban paths that cannot be used to serve resources in portlets. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.resource.id.banned.paths.regexp=.*/(?:META-INF|WEB-INF)/.*
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Portlet Coordination"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Portlet Coordination</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to specify how events are distributed. If the value is "layout-set", then events will be distributed to all portlets contained in a layout set. If the value is "layout", then events will be distributed to all portlets that are present in a layout. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.event.distribution=layout
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to specify how public render parameters are distributed. If the value is "layout-set", then public render parameters will be distributed to all portlets contained in a layout set. This will only work correctly if the property "layout.default.p_l_reset" is set to false. If the value is "layout", then public render parameters will be distributed to all portlets that are present in a layout. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.public.render.parameter.distribution=layout
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Portlet Filters"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Portlet Filters</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of portlet filters that will be applied to all portlets. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portlet.filters.system=com.liferay.portlet.ScriptDataPortletFilter
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Theme"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Theme</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to load the theme's merged CSS files for faster loading for production. </p> 
  <p>Set this property to false for easier debugging for development. You can also disable fast loading by setting the URL parameter "css_fast_load" to "0". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.css.fast.load=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to load the theme's merged image files for faster loading for production. </p> 
  <p>Set this property to false for easier debugging for development. You can also disable fast loading by setting the URL parameter "images_fast_load" to "0". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.images.fast.load=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to allow directly invoked JSPs to be overridden by a different version of the JSP that exists in a theme. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.jsp.override.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the theme's shortcut icon. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.shortcut.icon=favicon.ico
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to set the default virtual path for all hot deployed themes. See liferay-look-and-feel_6_1_0.dtd and the virtual-path element for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.virtual.path=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this with an absolute path to specify where imported theme files from a LAR will be stored. This path will override the file-storage path specified in liferay-theme-loader.xml. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.loader.storage.path=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Themes can be imported via LAR files. Set this to true if imported themes should use a new theme id on every import. This will ensure that a copy of the old theme is preserved in the theme loader storage path. However, this also means that a lot of themes that are no longer used remain in the file system. It is recommended that you set this to false. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.loader.new.theme.id.on.import=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to decorate portlets by default. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.portlet.decorate.default=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to exposing sharing icons for portlets by default. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    theme.portlet.sharing.default=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Resource Actions"></a>

  <pre class="defaults">    resource.actions.read.portlet.resources=true
</pre>

  <hr> 
  <a name="Spring"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Spring</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited Spring configurations. These will be loaded after the bean definitions specified in the contextConfigLocation parameter in web.xml. </p> 
  <p>Note that there is a special case for hibernate-spring.xml and jpa-spring.xml. Even though both files are specified, only one will actually load at runtime based on the property "persistence.provider". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    spring.configs=\
        META-INF/base-spring.xml,\
        \
        META-INF/hibernate-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/infrastructure-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/management-spring.xml,\
        \
        META-INF/util-spring.xml,\
        \
        META-INF/jpa-spring.xml,\
        \
        META-INF/executor-spring.xml,\
        \
        META-INF/audit-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/cluster-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/editor-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/jcr-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/ldap-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/messaging-core-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/messaging-misc-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/mobile-device-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/monitoring-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/notifications-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/poller-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/rules-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/scheduler-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/scripting-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/search-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/workflow-spring.xml,\
        \
        META-INF/counter-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/mail-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/portal-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/portlet-container-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/staging-spring.xml,\
        META-INF/virtual-layouts-spring.xml,\
        \
        #META-INF/dynamic-data-source-spring.xml,\
        #META-INF/shard-data-source-spring.xml,\
        #META-INF/memcached-spring.xml,\
        \
        META-INF/ext-spring.xml
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the bean name for the Liferay data source. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    spring.hibernate.data.source=liferayDataSource
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the bean name for the Liferay session factory. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    spring.hibernate.session.factory=&amp;liferaySessionFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to false to manually open and close sessions. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    spring.hibernate.session.delegated=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Persistence"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Persistence</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the provider used for ORM persistence. If this property is set to "jpa", then the properties with the prefix "jpa." will be read. If this property is set to "hibernate", then the properties with the prefix "hibernate." will be read. </p> 
  <p>Note that this property affects the loading of hibernate-spring.xml or jpa-spring.xml in the property "spring.configs". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    persistence.provider=hibernate
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    persistence.provider=jpa
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Hibernate"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Hibernate</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited Hibernate configurations. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hibernate.configs=\
        META-INF/mail-hbm.xml,\
        META-INF/portal-hbm.xml,\
        META-INF/ext-hbm.xml
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Liferay will automatically detect the Hibernate dialect in com.liferay.portal.spring.PortalHibernateConfiguration. Set this property to manually override the automatically detected dialect. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    hibernate.dialect=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the Hibernate connection release mode. You should not modify this unless you know what you're doing. The default setting works best for Spring managed transactions. See the method buildSessionFactory in class org.springframework.orm.hibernate3.LocalSessionFactoryBean and search for the phrase "on_close" to understand how this works. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    hibernate.connection.release_mode=on_close
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the Hibernate cache region factory. Ehcache is recommended in a clustered environment. See the property "net.sf.ehcache.configurationResourceName" for detailed configuration. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hibernate.cache.region.factory_class=com.liferay.portal.dao.orm.hibernate.region.SingletonLiferayEhcacheRegionFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>This property is used if Hibernate is configured to use Ehcache's region factory. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    net.sf.ehcache.configurationResourceName=/ehcache/hibernate-clustered.xml
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Configure this property if using Ehcache's default replication method for Hibernate's region cache. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    net.sf.ehcache.configurationResourceName.peerProviderProperties=peerDiscovery=automatic,multicastGroupAddress=${multicast.group.address["hibernate"]},multicastGroupPort=${multicast.group.port["hibernate"]},timeToLive=1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set other Hibernate cache settings. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hibernate.cache.use_query_cache=true
    hibernate.cache.use_second_level_cache=true
    hibernate.cache.use_minimal_puts=true
    hibernate.cache.use_structured_entries=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Uncomment these properties to disable Hibernate caching. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    hibernate.cache.use_query_cache=false
    hibernate.cache.use_second_level_cache=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the JDBC batch size to improve performance. </p> 
  <p>If you're using Hypersonic, you SHOULD set the batch size to 0 as a workaround for a logging bug in the Hypersonic driver. See LPS-5426 for more information. </p> 
  <p>If you're using Oracle 9i, you MUST set the batch size to 0 as a workaround for a hanging bug in the Oracle driver. See LEP-1234 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hibernate.jdbc.batch_size=20
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    hibernate.jdbc.batch_size=0
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set other miscellaneous Hibernate properties. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hibernate.jdbc.use_scrollable_resultset=true
    hibernate.bytecode.use_reflection_optimizer=true
    hibernate.show_sql=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Use the classic query factory until WebLogic and Hibernate 3 can get along. See http://www.hibernate.org/250.html#A23 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hibernate.query.factory_class=org.hibernate.hql.classic.ClassicQueryTranslatorFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to enable Hibernate cache monitoring. See LPS-2056 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    hibernate.generate_statistics=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="JPA"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>JPA</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to "none" to disable the JPA validation. Some application servers have the validation JARs in the global class path which causes conflicts with Hibernate. See LPS-22453 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javax.persistence.validation.mode=none
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited JPA configurations. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jpa.configs=\
        META-INF/mail-orm.xml,\
        META-INF/portal-orm.xml
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the name of the JPA provider. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jpa.provider=eclipselink
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jpa.provider=hibernate
    jpa.provider=openjpa
    jpa.provider=toplink
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify provider specific properties prefixed with "jpa.provider.property." </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jpa.provider.property.eclipselink.allow-zero-id=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jpa.provider.property.eclipselink.logging.level=FINEST
    jpa.provider.property.eclipselink.logging.timestamp=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The LoadTimeWeaver interface is a Spring class that allows JPA ClassTransformer instances to be plugged in a specific manner depending on the environment. </p> 
  <p>Not all JPA providers require a JVM agent (Hibernate is an example). If your provider does not require an agent or you have other alternatives (such as applying enhancements at build time through a custom compiler or an Ant task), then the loadtime weaver should not be used. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jpa.load.time.weaver=org.springframework.instrument.classloading.ReflectiveLoadTimeWeaver
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jpa.load.time.weaver=org.springframework.instrument.classloading.glassfish.GlassFishLoadTimeWeaver
    jpa.load.time.weaver=org.springframework.instrument.classloading.oc4j.OC4JLoadTimeWeaver
    jpa.load.time.weaver=org.springframework.instrument.classloading.weblogic.WebLogicLoadTimeWeaver
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify a specific database platform setting if the JPA provider is not able to detect the database platform. </p> 
  <p>Valid values for the Hibernate and OpenJPA providers are: DB2, DERBY, HSQL, INFORMIX, MYSQL, ORACLE, POSTGRESQL, SQL_SERVER, and SYBASE. </p> 
  <p>Valid values for the EclipseLink provider are: org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.DB2MainframePlatform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.DB2Platform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.DerbyPlatform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.HSQLPlatform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.InformixPlatform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.MySQLPlatform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.OraclePlatform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.PostgreSQLPlatform, org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.SQLServerPlatform, or org.eclipse.persistence.platform.database.SybasePlatform. </p> 
  <p>Check with JPA provider's documentation for details and all possible values. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jpa.database.platform=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Liferay will automatically detect the database type by initializing DBUtil. You can override the value here if needed. Expected values are: db2, derby, firebird, hypersonic, informix, ingres, interbase, jdatastore, mysql, oracle, postgresql, sap, sqlserver, and sybase. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jpa.database.type=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="JDBC"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>JDBC</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the JNDI name to lookup the JDBC data source. If none is set, then the portal will attempt to create the JDBC data source based on the properties prefixed with "jdbc.default.". </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.jndi.name=jdbc/LiferayPool
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the properties used to create the JDBC data source. These properties will only be read if the property "jdbc.default.jndi.name" is not set. </p> 
  <p>The default settings are configured for an in-memory database called Hypersonic that is not recommended for production use. Please change the properties to use another database. </p> 
  <p>Add dynamic-data-source-spring.xml to the property "spring.configs" to configure the portal to use one database cluster for read calls and another database cluster for write calls. The convention is to create a set of properties prefixed with "jdbc.read." to handle read calls and another set of properties prefixed with "jdbc.write." to handle write calls. These data sources can also be created via JNDI by setting the properties "jdbc.read.jndi.name" and "jdbc.write.jndi.name". Note that these settings, though separate, are a copy of the default settings with the newly overridden values. </p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>DB2 </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=com.ibm.db2.jcc.DB2Driver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:db2://localhost:50000/lportal:deferPrepares=false;fullyMaterializeInputStreams=true;fullyMaterializeLobData=true;progresssiveLocators=2;progressiveStreaming=2;
    jdbc.default.username=db2admin
    jdbc.default.password=lportal
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Derby </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=org.apache.derby.jdbc.EmbeddedDriver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:derby:lportal
    jdbc.default.username=
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Hypersonic </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=org.hsqldb.jdbcDriver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:hsqldb:${liferay.home}/data/hsql/lportal
    jdbc.default.username=sa
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Ingres </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=com.ingres.jdbc.IngresDriver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:ingres://localhost:II7/lportal
    jdbc.default.username=
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>MySQL </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=com.mysql.jdbc.Driver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost/lportal?useUnicode=true&amp;characterEncoding=UTF-8&amp;useFastDateParsing=false
    jdbc.default.username=
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Oracle </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=oracle.jdbc.driver.OracleDriver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:oracle:thin:@localhost:1521:xe
    jdbc.default.username=lportal
    jdbc.default.password=lportal
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>P6Spy </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=com.p6spy.engine.spy.P6SpyDriver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:mysql://localhost/lportal?useUnicode=true&amp;characterEncoding=UTF-8&amp;useFastDateParsing=false
    jdbc.default.username=
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>PostgreSQL </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=org.postgresql.Driver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:postgresql://localhost:5432/lportal
    jdbc.default.username=sa
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>SQL Server </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=net.sourceforge.jtds.jdbc.Driver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:jtds:sqlserver://localhost/lportal
    jdbc.default.username=sa
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Sybase </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.driverClassName=net.sourceforge.jtds.jdbc.Driver
    jdbc.default.url=jdbc:jtds:sybase://localhost:5000/lportal
    jdbc.default.username=sa
    jdbc.default.password=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Liferay can use C3PO, DBCP, or Tomcat for connection pooling. See com.liferay.portal.dao.jdbc.util.DataSourceFactoryBean for the actual implementation. It is important to understand the strengths and weaknesses of each provider so that you can choose the best one that fits your deployment scenario. Provider specific properties can also be passed along directly to the provider. For example, the property "jdbc.default.acquireIncrement" is read by C3PO, and the property "jdbc.default.maxActive" is read by DBCP. </p> 
  <p>The default provider is C3PO. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jdbc.default.liferay.pool.provider=c3po
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.liferay.pool.provider=dbcp
    jdbc.default.liferay.pool.provider=tomcat
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The following properties will be read by C3PO if Liferay is configured to use C3PO in the property "jdbc.default.liferay.pool.provider". See http://www.mchange.com/projects/c3p0/index.html#configuration for a list of additional fields used by C3PO for configuring database connections. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jdbc.default.acquireIncrement=5
    jdbc.default.acquireRetryAttempts=3
    jdbc.default.acquireRetryDelay=1000
    jdbc.default.connectionCustomizerClassName=com.liferay.portal.dao.jdbc.pool.c3p0.PortalConnectionCustomizer
    jdbc.default.idleConnectionTestPeriod=60
    jdbc.default.maxIdleTime=3600
    jdbc.default.maxPoolSize=100
    jdbc.default.minPoolSize=10
    jdbc.default.numHelperThreads=10
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.transactionIsolation=1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The following properties will be read by both DBCP and Tomcat JDBC Connection Pool if Liferay is configured to use DBCP or Tomcat JDBC Connection Pool in the property "jdbc.default.liferay.pool.provider". See http://commons.apache.org/dbcp/configuration.html and http://people.apache.org/~fhanik/jdbc-pool/jdbc-pool.html for a list of additional fields used by DBCP or Tomcat JDBC Connection Pool for configuring database connections. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jdbc.default.maxActive=100
    jdbc.default.minIdle=10
    jdbc.default.removeAbandonedTimeout=3600
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jdbc.default.defaultTransactionIsolation=READ_UNCOMMITTED
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The following properties will be read by Tomcat JDBC Connection Pool if Liferay is configured to use Tomcat JDBC Connection Pool in the property "jdbc.default.liferay.pool.provider". See http://people.apache.org/~fhanik/jdbc-pool/jdbc-pool.html for a list of additional fields used by Tomcat JDBC Connection Pool for configuring database connections. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jdbc.default.jdbcInterceptors=org.apache.tomcat.jdbc.pool.interceptor.ConnectionState
    jdbc.default.jmxEnabled=true
    jdbc.default.fairQueue=true
    jdbc.default.timeBetweenEvictionRunsMillis=30000
    jdbc.default.useEquals=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Custom SQL"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Custom SQL</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited custom SQL configurations. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    custom.sql.configs=custom-sql/default.xml
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Some databases do not recognize a NULL IS NULL check. Set the "custom.sql.function.isnull" and "custom.sql.function.isnotnull" properties for your specific database. </p> 
  <p>There is no need to manually set these properties because com.liferay.portal.spring.PortalHibernateConfiguration already sets it. However, these properties are available so that you can see how you can override it for a database that PortalHibernateConfiguration does not yet know how to auto configure. </p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>DB2 </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    custom.sql.function.isnull=CAST(? AS VARCHAR(32672)) IS NULL
    custom.sql.function.isnotnull=CAST(? AS VARCHAR(32672)) IS NOT NULL
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>MySQL (for testing only) </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    custom.sql.function.isnull=IFNULL(?, '1') = '1'
    custom.sql.function.isnotnull=IFNULL(?, '1') = '0'
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Sybase </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    custom.sql.function.isnull=CONVERT(VARCHAR,?) IS NULL
    custom.sql.function.isnotnull=CONVERT(VARCHAR,?) IS NOT NULL
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Database"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Database</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to update database indexes on startup. This will ensure that all necessary indexes are added and that unnecessary indexes are removed. Only indexes that have names that match "LIFERAY_" OR "IX_" will be updated. Make sure that your custom indexes do not match the Liferay pattern to ensure that your custom indexes are not removed as unnecessary indexes. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    database.indexes.update.on.startup=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify any database vendor specific settings. </p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>MySQL </p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the MySQL engine type. InnoDB is the recommended engine because it provides transactional integrity. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    database.mysql.engine=InnoDB
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Transaction"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Transaction</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the transaction isolation level for the Counter service. See "transaction.isolation.portal" for more information. The preferred value is 8 when the transaction manager supports it. If the transaction manager does not support it, (i.e. when using JPA and JpaTransactionManager) set this to -1 to use the database's default isolation level. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    transaction.isolation.counter=8
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the definition of the "portal" transaction isolation level. The "portal" transaction isolation level is not a real isolation level. It is just a pointer to a real isolation level that can be configured by setting this property. Set the value to -1 to use the database's default isolation level. Set the value to 2 to use "read committed". Set the value to 1 to use "read uncommitted". Set the value to 4 to use "repeatable read". Set the value to 8 to use "serializable". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    transaction.isolation.portal=2
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the transaction manager. It must be a class that extends org.springframework.transaction.support.AbstractPlatformTransactionManager. </p> 
  <p>The application server specific transaction managers provide XA transactions by leveraging application server specific data sources and thus require additional application server specific configuration. You should not modify this unless you know what you're doing. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    transaction.manager.impl=com.liferay.portal.spring.hibernate.LastSessionRecorderHibernateTransactionManager
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    transaction.manager.impl=org.springframework.transaction.jta.JtaTransactionManager
    transaction.manager.impl=org.springframework.transaction.jta.OC4JJtaTransactionManager
    transaction.manager.impl=org.springframework.transaction.jta.WebLogicJtaTransactionManager
    transaction.manager.impl=org.springframework.transaction.jta.WebSphereUowTransactionManager
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Additional properties that follow the pattern "transaction.manager.property.*" will be read to call the setters on the transaction manager. For example, the property "transaction.manager.property.globalRollbackOnParticipationFailure", will call the setter "setGlobalRollbackOnParticipationFailure" on the transaction manager. The list of available setters depends on the implementation specified in the property "transaction.manager.impl". </p> 
  <p>"allowCustomIsolationLevels" should be set to true when using the JtaTransactionManager. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    transaction.manager.property.globalRollbackOnParticipationFailure=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    transaction.manager.property.allowCustomIsolationLevels=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Transactional Cache"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Transactional Cache</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to enable transactional cache. When enabled, changes to caches take effect when transaction commits successfully. Caches rollback when transactions rollback. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    transactional.cache.enable=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Sharded Databases"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Sharded Databases</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the database that is to be used for the default company and globally used tables in a sharded environment. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    shard.default.name=default
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify an algorithm for selecting a new shard on portal instance creation. Use ManualShardSelector for shard selection via the web interface. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    shard.selector=com.liferay.portal.dao.shard.RoundRobinShardSelector
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    shard.selector=com.liferay.portal.dao.shard.ManualShardSelector
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Ehcache"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Ehcache</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the classpath to the location of the Ehcache config file for internal caches. Edit the file specified in the property "ehcache.multi-vm.config.location" to enable clustered cache. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.single.vm.config.location=/ehcache/liferay-single-vm.xml
    ehcache.multi.vm.config.location=/ehcache/liferay-multi-vm-clustered.xml
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Uncomment the following in a clustered environment. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.multi.vm.config.location.peerProviderProperties=peerDiscovery=automatic,multicastGroupAddress=${multicast.group.address["multi-vm"]},multicastGroupPort=${multicast.group.port["multi-vm"]},timeToLive=1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a class name that extends net.sf.ehcache.bootstrap.BootstrapCacheLoaderFactory. This class is used by Ehcache to determine how caches communicate with each other in a clustered environment. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.bootstrap.cache.loader.factory=net.sf.ehcache.distribution.RMIBootstrapCacheLoaderFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ehcache.bootstrap.cache.loader.factory=com.liferay.portal.cache.ehcache.JGroupsBootstrapCacheLoaderFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a class name that extends net.sf.ehcache.event.CacheEventListenerFactory. This class is used by Ehcache to determine how caches communicate with each other in a clustered environment. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.cache.event.listener.factory=net.sf.ehcache.distribution.RMICacheReplicatorFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ehcache.cache.event.listener.factory=net.sf.ehcache.distribution.jgroups.JGroupsCacheReplicatorFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a class name that extends net.sf.ehcache.distribution.CacheManagerPeerProviderFactory. This class is used by Ehcache to determine how caches communicate with each other in a clustered environment. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.cache.manager.peer.provider.factory=net.sf.ehcache.distribution.RMICacheManagerPeerProviderFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ehcache.cache.manager.peer.provider.factory=net.sf.ehcache.distribution.jgroups.JGroupsCacheManagerPeerProviderFactory
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable JMX integration in com.liferay.portal.cache.EhcachePortalCacheManager. Set this to false if the portal needs to be reloaded under WebSphere. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.portal.cache.manager.jmx.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow Ehcache to use blocking caches. This improves performance significantly by locking on keys instead of the entire cache. The drawback is that threads can hang if the cache is not used properly. Make sure that all queries that return a miss also immediately populate the cache, or else other threads that are blocked on a query of that same key will continue to hang. Reference Ehcache's BlockingCache for more information. The blocking cache is no longer implemented by Ehcache's BlockingCache, but by Liferay's BlockingPortalCache for better safety and faster performance. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.blocking.cache.allowed=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable Ehcache statistics. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.statistics.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the socket timeout in milliseconds. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.socket.so.timeout=10000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the start port for Ehcache socket. The port number will increase by 1 until it finds an unused port. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ehcache.socket.start.port=32454
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="JavaScript"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>JavaScript</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set a list of JavaScript files that will be loaded automatically in /html/common/themes/top_js.jsp. </p> 
  <p>There are two lists of files specified in the properties "javascript.barebone.files" and "javascript.everything.files". </p> 
  <p>As the name suggests, the barebone list is the minimum list of JavaScript files required for most cases. The everything list includes everything else not listed in the barebone list. </p> 
  <p>The two lists of files exist for performance reasons because unauthenticated users usually do not utilize all the JavaScript that is available. See the property "javascript.barebone.enabled" for more information on the logic of when the barebone list is used and when the everything list is used and how to customize that logic. </p> 
  <p>The list of files are also merged and packed for further performance improvements. See the property "javascript.fast.load" for more details. </p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the list of barebone files. </p> 
  <p>The ordering of the JavaScript files is important. </p> 
  <p>The Liferay scripts are grouped in such a way, that the first grouping denotes utility scripts that are used by the second and third groups. The second grouping denotes utility classes that rely on the first group, but does not rely on the second or third group. The third grouping denotes modules that rely on the first and second group. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javascript.barebone.files=\
        \
        #
        # YUI core
        #
        \
        aui/yui/yui.js,\
        \
        #
        # YUI modules
        #
        \
        aui/arraylist-add/arraylist-add.js,\

        aui/arraylist/arraylist.js,\

        aui/aui-overlay/aui-overlay-manager.js,\
        aui/aui-overlay/aui-overlay-mask.js,\
        aui/aui-parse-content/aui-parse-content.js,\
        \
        #
        # Liferay modules
        #
        \
        liferay/address.js,\
        liferay/dockbar.js,\
        liferay/layout_configuration.js,\
        liferay/layout_exporter.js,\
        liferay/session.js,\
        \
        #
        # Deprecated JS
        #
        \
        liferay/deprecated.js
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to false to always load JavaScript files listed in the property "javascript.everything.files". Set this to true to sometimes load "javascript.barebone.files" and sometimes load "javascript.everything.files". </p> 
  <p>The default logic is coded in com.liferay.portal.events.ServicePreAction in such a way that unauthenticated users get the list of barebone JavaScript files whereas authenticated users get both the list of barebone JavaScript files and the list of everything JavaScript files. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javascript.barebone.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true to load the packed version of files listed in the properties "javascript.barebone.files" or "javascript.everything.files". </p> 
  <p>Set this property to false for easier debugging for development. You can also disable fast loading by setting the URL parameter "js_fast_load" to "0". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javascript.fast.load=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited properties that are valid bundle ids for the JavaScript minifier. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javascript.bundle.ids=\
        javascript.barebone.files,\
        javascript.everything.files
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Define a bundle directory for each property listed in "javascript.bundle.ids". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javascript.bundle.dir[javascript.barebone.files]=/html/js
    javascript.bundle.dir[javascript.everything.files]=/html/js
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Define the bundle dependencies using any property listed in "javascript.bundle.ids". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javascript.bundle.dependencies[javascript.everything.files]=javascript.barebone.files
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable the display of JavaScript logging. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    javascript.log.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p>

  <a name="Company"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Company</h3> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.default.name=Liferay
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>This sets the default web id. Omniadmin users must belong to the company with this web id. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.default.web.id=liferay.com
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>This sets the default home URL of the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.default.home.url=/web/guest
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>This sets the default locale of the portal, overriding the properties "user.language" and "user.country" specified in system.properties. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    company.default.locale=en_US
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>This sets the default time zone of the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.default.time.zone=UTC
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to the appropriate encryption algorithm to be used for company level encryption algorithms (except password encryption which is defined via the property "passwords.encryption.algorithm"). </p> 
  <p>If you change this setting, you may need to also change the property "company.encryption.key.size" to configure the desired encryption key size. </p> 
  <p>For more details about encryption keys, see the Java Cryptography Extension documentation. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.encryption.algorithm=DES
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    company.encryption.algorithm=AES
    company.encryption.algorithm=ARCFOUR
    company.encryption.algorithm=Blowfish
    company.encryption.algorithm=DESede
    company.encryption.algorithm=HmacMD5
    company.encryption.algorithm=HmacSHA1
    company.encryption.algorithm=HmacSHA256
    company.encryption.algorithm=HmacSHA384
    company.encryption.algorithm=HmacSHA512
    company.encryption.algorithm=RC2
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to define the size used for the company wide encryption key. If you change this setting, you may need to also change the property "company.encryption.algorithm" to ensure the algorithm supports your key size. </p> 
  <p>For more details about supported key sizes for encryption keys, see the Java Cryptography Extension documentation </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.encryption.key.size=56
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    company.encryption.key.size=128
    company.encryption.key.size=168
    company.encryption.key.size=256
    company.encryption.key.size=384
    company.encryption.key.size=512
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The login field is prepopulated with the company's domain name if the login is unpopulated and user authentication is based on email addresses. Set this to false to disable the behavior. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.login.prepopulate.domain=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The portal can authenticate users based on their email address, screen name, or user id. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.auth.type=emailAddress
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    company.security.auth.type=screenName
    company.security.auth.type=userId
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to ensure users login with https. If this is set to true and you want your HTTP session to contain your credentials after logging in, then the property "session.enable.phishing.protection" must be set to false or your credentials will only be available in the HTTPS session. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.auth.requires.https=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow users to select the "remember me" feature to automatically login to the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.auto.login=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to the maximum age (in number of seconds) of the browser cookie that enables the "remember me" feature. A value of 31536000 signifies lifespan of one year. A value of -1 signifies a lifespan of a browser session. </p> 
  <p>Rather than setting this to 0, set the property "company.security.auto.login" to false to disable the "remember me" feature. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.auto.login.max.age=31536000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow users to autocomplete the login form based on their previously entered values. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.login.form.autocomplete=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow users to ask the portal to send them their password. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.send.password=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow users to ask the portal to send them a password reset link. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.send.password.reset.link=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow strangers to create accounts and register themselves on the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.strangers=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Enter a friendly URL of a page that will be used to create new accounts whenever the user clicks the "create account" link in the login portlet. This allows providing custom portlets to create accounts. By default, the portal's create account will be used. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    company.security.strangers.url=/create_account
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if strangers can create accounts with email addresses that match the company mail suffix. This property is not used unless "company.security.strangers" is also set to true. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.strangers.with.mx=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if strangers who create accounts need to be verified via email. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.strangers.verify=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow site administrators to use their own logo instead of the enterprise logo. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    company.security.site.logo=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of sections that will be included as part of the company settings form. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>

  <hr>

</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to always autogenerate user screen names even if the user gives a specific user screen name. If this is set to true, the LDAP importer will fetch users by their email address even if the property "company.security.auth.type" is set to screenName. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.screen.name.always.autogenerate=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a class name that implements com.liferay.portal.security.auth.ScreenNameGenerator. This class will be called to generate user screen names. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.screen.name.generator=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.DefaultScreenNameGenerator
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a class name that implements com.liferay.portal.security.auth.ScreenNameValidator. This class will be called to validate user screen names. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.screen.name.validator=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.DefaultScreenNameValidator
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    users.screen.name.validator=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LiberalScreenNameValidator
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to false if you want to be able to create users without an email address. An email address will be automatically assigned to a user based on the property "users.email.address.auto.suffix". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.email.address.required=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the suffix of the email address that will be automatically generated for a user that does not have an email address. This property is not used unless the property "users.email.address.required" is set to false. The autogenerated email address will be the user id plus the specified suffix. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.email.address.auto.suffix=@no-emailaddress.com
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a class name that implements com.liferay.portal.security.auth.EmailAddressGenerator. This class will be called to generate an email address for a user that does not specify an email address. This class will only be used if the property "users.email.address.required" is set to false. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.email.address.generator=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.DefaultEmailAddressGenerator
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a class name that implements com.liferay.portal.security.auth.EmailAddressValidator. This class will be called to validate user email addresses. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.email.address.validator=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.DefaultEmailAddressValidator
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    users.email.address.validator=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LiberalEmailAddressValidator
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if you want the last name to be required when creating users. </p>

</pre>
  <p></p>

  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    users.full.name.validator=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.DefaultFullNameValidator
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the maximum file size for user portraits. A value of 0 for the maximum file size can be used to indicate unlimited file size. However, the maximum file size allowed is set in the property "com.liferay.portal.upload.UploadServletRequestImpl.max.size". </p>
