  <hr> 
  <a name="Groups and Roles"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Groups and Roles</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited system group names that will exist in addition to the standard system groups. When the server starts, the portal checks to ensure all system groups exist. Any missing system group will be created by the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.groups=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited system role names that will exist in addition to the standard system roles. When the server starts, the portal checks to ensure all system roles exist. Any missing system role will be created by the portal. </p> 
  <p>The standard system roles are: Administrator, Guest, Power User, and User. These roles cannot be removed or renamed. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.roles=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Administrator system role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.role.Administrator.description=Administrators are super users who can do anything.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Guest system role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.role.Guest.description=Unauthenticated users always have this role.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Owner system role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.role.Owner.description=This is an implied role with respect to the objects users create.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Power User system role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.role.Power.User.description=Power Users have their own personal site.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the User system role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.role.User.description=Authenticated users should be assigned this role.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited system organization role names that will exist in addition to the standard system organization roles. When the server starts, the portal checks to ensure all system organization roles exist. Any missing system organization role will be created by the portal. </p> 
  <p>The standard system organization roles are: Organization Administrator, Organization Member, and Organization Owner. These roles cannot be removed or renamed. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.organization.roles=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Organization Administrator system organization role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.organization.role.Organization.Administrator.description=Organization Administrators are super users of their organization but cannot make other users into Organization Administrators.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Organization Member system organization role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.organization.role.Organization.User.description=All users who belong to an organization have this role within that organization.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Organization Owner system organization role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.organization.role.Organization.Owner.description=Organization Owners are super users of their organization and can assign organization roles to users.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited system site role names that will exist in addition to the standard system site roles. When the server starts, the portal checks to ensure all system site roles exist. Any missing system site role will be created by the portal. </p> 
  <p>The standard system site roles are: Site Administrator, Site Member, and Site Owner. These roles cannot be removed or renamed. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.site.roles=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Site Administrator system site role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.site.role.Site.Administrator.description=Site Administrators are super users of their site but cannot make other users into Site Administrators.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Site Member system site role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.site.role.Site.Member.description=All users who belong to a site have this role within that site.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the description of the Site Owner system site role. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    system.site.role.Site.Owner.description=Site Owners are super users of their site and can assign site roles to users.
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Omniadmin users can administer the portal's core functionality: gc, shutdown, etc. Omniadmin users must belong to the default company. </p> 
  <p>Multiple portal instances might be deployed on one application server, and not all of the administrators should have access to this core functionality. Input the ids of users who are omniadmin users. </p> 
  <p>Leave this field blank if users who belong to the right company and have the Administrator role are allowed to administer the portal's core functionality. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    omniadmin.users=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if all users are required to agree to the terms of use. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    terms.of.use.required=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the group id and the article id of the Journal article that will be displayed as the terms of use. The default text will be used if no Journal article is specified. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    terms.of.use.journal.article.group.id=
    terms.of.use.journal.article.id=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify subtypes of roles if you want to be able to search for roles using your custom criteria. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    roles.site.subtypes=
    roles.organization.subtypes=
    roles.regular.subtypes=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true when you want the validation to allow for creation of roles with numeric names. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    roles.name.allow.numeric=false
</pre>

  <a name="Organizations"></a>

  <p>Set this property to false if you want any administrator of an organization to be able to assign any user to that organization. By default, he will only be able to assign the users of the organizations and suborganizations that he can manage. </p>

</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to true if you want users to only be members of the organizations to which they are assigned explicitly. By default they will also become implicit members of the ancestors of those organizations. for example if a user belongs to Liferay Spain he will implicitly be a member of the ancestors Liferay Europe and Liferay Global and will be able to access their private pages. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>

</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to search organizations from the index. Set this to false to search organizations from the database. Note that setting this to false will disable the ability to search organizations based on Expando attributes. This setting is not used unless the property "organizations.indexer.enabled" is set to true. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>

  <hr> 
  <a name="Languages and Time Zones"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Languages and Time Zones</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the available locales. Messages corresponding to a specific language are specified in properties files with file names matching that of content/Language_*.properties. These values can also be overridden in properties files with file names matching that of content/Language-ext_*.properties. Use a comma to separate each entry. </p> 
  <p>If there is more than one locale for the same language, the first one in the list will be used when a translation is requested in another locale of the same language but a translated value cannot be found. For example, if there are two locales such us pt_BR and pt_PT (in this order), any key not found in pt_PT will be looked for in pt_BR. </p> 
  <p>Language codes follow the ISO 639-1 standard. Content for each locale must be UTF-8 encoded. </p> 
  <p>See the following links, which specify language and country codes: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     http://www.loc.gov/standards/iso639-2/php/code_list.php
     http://userpage.chemie.fu-berlin.de/diverse/doc/ISO_3166.html
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    locales=ar_SA,eu_ES,bg_BG,ca_AD,ca_ES,zh_CN,zh_TW,hr_HR,cs_CZ,da_DK,nl_NL,nl_BE,en_US,en_GB,et_EE,fi_FI,fr_FR,gl_ES,de_DE,el_GR,iw_IL,hi_IN,hu_HU,in_ID,it_IT,ja_JP,ko_KR,lo_LA,nb_NO,fa_IR,pl_PL,pt_BR,pt_PT,ro_RO,ru_RU,sr_RS,sr_RS_latin,sl_SI,sk_SK,es_ES,sv_SE,tr_TR,uk_UA,vi_VN
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the locales that are in beta. Go to http://translate.liferay.com to participate in the translation efforts. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    locales.beta=ar_SA,eu_ES,bg_BG,ca_AD,ca_ES,zh_TW,hr_HR,cs_CZ,da_DK,nl_NL,nl_BE,en_GB,et_EE,fi_FI,fr_FR,gl_ES,el_GR,iw_IL,hi_IN,in_ID,it_IT,ja_JP,ko_KR,lo_LA,nb_NO,fa_IR,pl_PL,pt_PT,ro_RO,ru_RU,sr_RS,sr_RS_latin,sl_SI,sk_SK,sv_SE,tr_TR,uk_UA,vi_VN
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if unauthenticated users get their preferred language from the Accept-Language header. Set this to false if unauthenticated users get their preferred language from their company. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    locale.default.request=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to 0 if the locale is not automatically prepended to a URL. This means that each URL could potentially point to many different languages. For example, the URL http://localhost:8080/web/guest/home could then be viewed by users in many different languages. </p> 
  <p>Set this to 1 if the locale is automatically prepended to a URL when the requested locale is not the default locale. This means that each URL points to just one language. For example, the URL http://localhost:8080/web/guest/home would point to the default language. The URL http://localhost:8080/zh/web/guest/home and http://localhost:8080/zh_CN/web/guest/home would both point to the Chinese language. </p> 
  <p>In cases where the prepended locale is "zh" and not complete locale "zh_CN", then the full locale returned will be based on the order in which the locales appear in the property "locales". If "zh_CN" appears before "zh_TW", then "zh" will be a short hand for "zh_TW". </p> 
  <p>The default language is set in system.properties with the properties "user.country" and "user.language". </p> 
  <p>Set this to 2 if the locale is automatically prepended to every URL. This means that each URL points to just one language. </p> 
  <p>Note that each language requires an entry in the property "locales" and a servlet mapping in web.xml for the I18n Servlet. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    locale.prepend.friendly.url.style=1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to disable language translations. When a translation is requested for the key "first-name", instead of returning "First Name" in English (or in its relevant locale), it will return "first-name". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    translations.disabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the available time zones. The specified ids must match those from the class java.util.TimeZone. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    time.zones=\
        Pacific/Midway,\
        Pacific/Honolulu,\
        America/Anchorage,\
        America/Los_Angeles,\
        America/Denver,\
        America/Chicago,\
        America/New_York,\
        America/Caracas,\
        America/Puerto_Rico,\
        America/St_Johns,\
        America/Sao_Paulo,\
        America/Noronha,\
        Atlantic/Azores,\
        UTC,\
        Europe/Lisbon,\
        Europe/Paris,\
        Europe/Istanbul,\
        Asia/Jerusalem,\
        Asia/Baghdad,\
        Asia/Tehran,\
        Asia/Dubai,\
        Asia/Kabul,\
        Asia/Karachi,\
        Asia/Calcutta,\
        Asia/Katmandu,\
        Asia/Dhaka,\
        Asia/Rangoon,\
        Asia/Saigon,\
        Asia/Shanghai,\
        Asia/Tokyo,\
        Asia/Seoul,\
        Australia/Darwin,\
        Australia/Sydney,\
        Pacific/Guadalcanal,\
        Pacific/Auckland,\
        Pacific/Enderbury,\
        Pacific/Kiritimati
</pre>
  <p></p>

  <a name="Request"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Request</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Portlets that have been configured to use private request attributes in liferay-portlet.xml may still want to share some request attributes. This property allows you to configure which request attributes will be shared. Set a comma delimited list of attribute names that will be shared when the attribute name starts with one of the specified attribute names. For example, if you set the value to "hello_,world_", then all attribute names that start with "hello_" or "world_" will be shared. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    request.shared.attributes=LIFERAY_SHARED_
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Session"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Session</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the maximum number of key value pairs that can be stored in the session via SessionClicks. See LPS-20096 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.clicks.max.allowed.values=1024
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the maximun size of key and value terms that can be stored in the session via SessionClicks. See LPS-20096 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.clicks.max.size.terms=1024
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the delimiter for parsing compound session ids. </p> 
  <p>This addresses an issue with Weblogic and all application servers where the application server appends a unique JVM code to the session id. See LPS-18587. </p> 
  <p>Set a blank delimiter for the portal to attempt to detect a delimiter based on the application server. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.id.delimiter=
    session.id.weblogic.delimiter=!
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the maximum number of sessions allowed. A value of 0 or less than 0 will mean that there is no limit. A value greater than 0 will limit the number of sessions by invalidating newer sessions. </p> 
  <p>This property is not used unless the session max allowed filter is enabled. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.max.allowed=0
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the number of minutes before a session expires. This value is always overridden by the value set in web.xml. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.timeout=30
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the number of minutes before a warning is sent to the user informing the user of the session expiration. Specify 0 to disable any warnings. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.timeout.warning=1
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the auto-extend mode to true to avoid having to ask the user whether to extend the session or not. Instead it will be automatically extended. The purpose of this mode is to keep the session open as long as the user browser is open and with a portal page loaded. It is recommended to use this setting along with a smaller "session.timeout", such as 5 minutes for better performance. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.timeout.auto.extend=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if the user is redirected to the default page when the session expires. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.timeout.redirect.on.expire=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Portlets that have been configured to use private session attributes in liferay-portlet.xml may still want to share some session attributes. This property allows you to configure which session attributes will be shared. Set a comma delimited list of attribute names that will be shared when the attribute name starts with one of the specified attribute names. For example, if you set the value to "hello_,world_", then all attribute names that start with "hello_" or "world_" will be shared. </p> 
  <p>Note that this property is used to specify the sharing of session attributes from the portal to the portlet. This is not used to specify session sharing between portlet WARs or from the portlet to the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.shared.attributes=COMPANY_,LIFERAY_SHARED_,org.apache.struts.action.LOCALE,PORTLET_RENDER_PARAMETERS_,PUBLIC_RENDER_PARAMETERS_POOL_,USER_
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Explicitly exclude attributes that are shared from the portal to portlets. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.shared.attributes.excludes=USER_PASSWORD
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to store the user's password in the session. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.store.password=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to false to disable all persistent cookies. Features like automatically logging in will not work. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.enable.persistent.cookies=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable sessions when cookies are disabled. See LEP-4787. This behavior is configurable because enabling it can break certain setups. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.enable.url.with.session.id=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The login process sets several cookies if persistent cookies are enabled. Set this property to set the domain of those cookies. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    session.cookie.domain=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to use the full hostname for cookie domain values. By default the domain is trimmed to use only the root domain to allow cross domain logins. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.cookie.use.full.hostname=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to invalidate the session when a user logs into the portal. This helps prevents phishing. Set this to false if you need the guest user and the authenticated user to have the same session. </p> 
  <p>Set this to false if the property "company.security.auth.requires.https" is set to true and you want to maintain the same credentials across HTTP and HTTPS sessions. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.enable.phishing.protection=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set a comma delimited list of attribute names that will be copied to the new session when the property "session.enable.phishing.protection" is set to true. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.phishing.protected.attributes=HTTPS_INITIAL,LAST_PATH
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to test whether users have cookie support before allowing them to sign in. This test will always fail if "tck.url" is set to true because that property disables session cookies. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.test.cookie.support=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to allow com.liferay.portal.kernel.servlet.SerializableSessionAttributeListener to test if an added session variable is serializable. Unserializable values stored into the session will cause a session to not replicate if session replication was enabled by the application server. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.verify.serializable.attribute=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to disable sessions. Doing this will use cookies to remember the user across requests. This is useful if you want to scale very large sites where the user may be sent to a different server for each request. The drawback to this approach is that you must not rely on the API for sessions provided by the servlet and portlet specs. </p> 
  <p>This feature is only available for Tomcat and requires that you set Tomcat's Manager class to "com.liferay.support.tomcat.session.SessionLessManagerBase". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.disabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class names that extend com.liferay.portal.struts.SessionAction. These classes will run at the specified event. </p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Servlet session create event </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    servlet.session.create.events=com.liferay.portal.events.SessionCreateAction
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Servlet session destroy event </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    servlet.session.destroy.events=com.liferay.portal.events.SessionDestroyAction,com.liferay.portal.events.ChannelSessionDestroyAction
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to track user clicks in memory for the duration of a user's session. Setting this to true allows you to view all live sessions in the Admin portlet. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.tracker.memory.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to track user clicks in the database after a user's session is invalidated. Setting this to true allows you to generate usage reports from the database. Use this cautiously because this will store a lot of usage data. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.tracker.persistence.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to convert the tracked paths to friendly URLs. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.tracker.friendly.paths.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Enter a list of comma delimited paths that should not be tracked. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    session.tracker.ignore.paths=\
        /portal/render_portlet,\
        \
        /document_library/get_file
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="JAAS"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>JAAS</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to false to disable JAAS security checks. Disabling JAAS speeds up login. JAAS must be disabled if administrators are to be able to impersonate other users. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.jaas.enable=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>JAAS can authenticate users based on their email address, screen name, user id, or login as determined by the property "company.security.auth.type". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.jaas.auth.type=userId
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    portal.jaas.auth.type=emailAddress
    portal.jaas.auth.type=screenName
    portal.jaas.auth.type=login
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>By default, com.liferay.portal.security.jaas.PortalLoginModule loads the correct JAAS login module based on what application server or servlet container the portal is deployed on. Set a JAAS implementation class to override this behavior. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    portal.jaas.impl=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The JAAS process may pass in an encrypted password and the authentication will only succeed if there is an exact match. Set this property to false to relax that behavior so the user can input an unencrypted password. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.jaas.strict.password=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable administrators to impersonate other users. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.impersonation.enable=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="JNDI"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>JNDI</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the configuration values for the JNDI context. Any property prefixed with "jndi.environment" will be passed to the JNDI context as an environment variable. The valid values are those specified in javax.naming.Context. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    jndi.environment.java.naming.security.credentials=
    jndi.environment.java.naming.security.principal=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Security Manager"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Security Manager</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this property to "default" to use the default security manager configured by the application server. A security manager will not be used if the application server did not configure one. </p> 
  <p>Set this property to "liferay" to use Liferay's security manager if the application server has not configured a security manager. </p> 
  <p>Set this property to "none" to explicitly remove the security manager regardless of whether one is configured. This ensures that the portal is run in a JVM without a security manager. </p> 
  <p>Set this property to "smart" to allow the portal, on startup, to decide which strategy to use based on which application server it is on. At runtime, the portal will attempt to override the current security manager with the portal security manager if a plugin is deployed that requires security management. Plugins require security management if it has the property "security-manager-enabled" set to true in liferay-plugin-package.properties. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.security.manager.strategy=smart
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the PACL policy checker to use for checking a security manager permission. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[com.liferay.portal.kernel.security.pacl.permission.PortalHookPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.PortalHookChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[com.liferay.portal.kernel.security.pacl.permission.PortalMessageBusPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.PortalMessageBusChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[com.liferay.portal.kernel.security.pacl.permission.PortalRuntimePermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.PortalRuntimeChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[com.liferay.portal.kernel.security.pacl.permission.PortalServicePermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.PortalServiceChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.awt.AWTPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.AWTChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.io.FilePermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.FileChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.io.SerializablePermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultRejectChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.lang.RuntimePermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.RuntimeChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.lang.reflect.ReflectPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.ReflectChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.net.NetPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.NetChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.net.SocketPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.SocketChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.security.SecurityPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.SecurityChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.sql.SQLPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultRejectChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.management.MBeanPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.MBeanChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.management.MBeanServerPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.MBeanChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.management.MBeanTrustPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.MBeanChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.management.remote.SubjectDelegationPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.MBeanChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.net.ssl.SSLPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultRejectChecker
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.lang.management.ManagementPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.security.AllPermission]=
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.security.UnresolvedPermission]=
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.util.PropertyPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[java.util.logging.LoggingPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.security.auth.AuthPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.security.auth.PrivateCredentialPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.security.auth.kerberos.DelegationPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.security.auth.kerberos.ServicePermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
    portal.security.manager.pacl.policy.checker[javax.sound.sampled.AudioPermission]=com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.DefaultAcceptChecker
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the default read paths used by com.liferay.portal.security.pacl.checker.FileChecker. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.security.manager.file.checker.default.read.paths[glassfish]=\
        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}html/common/-,\
        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}html/taglib/-
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em>

  <pre class="defaults">    portal.security.manager.file.checker.default.read.paths[geronimo]=\
        ${org.apache.geronimo.home.dir}/var/shared/-
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.security.manager.file.checker.default.read.paths[jetty]=\
        ${liferay.web.portal.dir},\
        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}html/common/-,\
        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}html/taglib/-
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.security.manager.file.checker.default.read.paths[weblogic]=\
        ${auto.deploy.installed.dir}/${plugin.servlet.context.name}/-,\
        ${auto.deploy.installed.dir}/ROOT/html/common/-,\
        ${auto.deploy.installed.dir}/ROOT/html/taglib/-

  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>

        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}html/common/-,\

        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}WEB-INF/classes,\
        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}WEB-INF/classes/html/common/-,\
        ${liferay.web.portal.dir}WEB-INF/classes/html/taglib/-
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the list of classes that will be preloaded by the PreloadClassloader to be made available to plugins when the portal security manager is enabled. These classes will be exempt from the security checks that result from class loading. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    portal.security.manager.preload.classloader.classes=\
        org.aopalliance.aop.Advice,\
        org.springframework.aop.Advisor,\
        org.springframework.aop.SpringProxy,\
        org.springframework.aop.TargetSource,\
        org.springframework.aop.framework.Advised,\
        org.springframework.aop.framework.AopConfigException,\
        org.springframework.jmx.export.MBeanExporter
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="LDAP"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>LDAP</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the values used to connect to a LDAP store. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.factory.initial=com.sun.jndi.ldap.LdapCtxFactory
    ldap.referral=follow
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Settings for com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LDAPAuth can be configured from the Admin portlet. It provides out-of-the-box support for Apache Directory Server, Microsoft Active Directory Server, Novell eDirectory, and OpenLDAP. The default settings are for Apache Directory Server. </p> 
  <p>The LDAPAuth class must be specified in the property "auth.pipeline.pre" to be executed. </p> 
  <p>Encryption is implemented by com.liferay.util.Encryptor.provider.class in system.properties. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.auth.enabled=false
    ldap.auth.required=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the page size for directory servers that support paging. This value needs to be 1000 or less for Microsoft Active Directory Server. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.page.size=1000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the number of values to return in each query to a multivalued attribute for directory servers that support range retrieval. The range size must be 1000 or less for Windows 2000 and 1500 or less for Windows Server 2003. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.range.size=1000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set either bind or password-compare for the LDAP authentication method. Bind is preferred by most vendors so that you don't have to worry about encryption strategies. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.auth.method=bind
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.auth.method=password-compare
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the password encryption to use for comparing passwords during import and to use for encrypting passwords during export. Comparing passwords during import will only be used when the property "ldap.auth.method" is set to password-compare. If the encryption is set to NONE, which is the default value, passwords are considered as plain text. The SHA-512 algorithm is currently unsupported. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=NONE
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=BCRYPT
    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=MD2
    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=MD5
    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=SHA
    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=SHA-256
    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=SHA-384
    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=SSHA
    ldap.auth.password.encryption.algorithm=UFC-CRYPT
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>You can write your own class that implements com.liferay.portal.security.ldap.AttributesTransformer to transform the LDAP attributes before a user or group is imported to the LDAP store. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.attrs.transformer.impl=com.liferay.portal.security.ldap.DefaultAttributesTransformer
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify the settings for LDAP connections. Any property prefixed with "ldap.connection." will be passed to the LDAP context as an environment variable. </p> 
  <p>To enable LDAP connection pooling, you have to set "ldap.connection.com.sun.jndi.ldap.connect.pool" to true and provide additional JVM system properties via the JVM start-up options via: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     java ... -Dcom.sun.jndi.ldap.connect.pool.maxsize=50 -Dcom.sun.jndi.ldap.connect.pool.timeout=10000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <p>See the following link: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     http://docs.oracle.com/javase/6/docs/technotes/guides/jndi/jndi-ldap.html#POOL
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.connection.com.sun.jndi.ldap.connect.pool=true
    ldap.connection.com.sun.jndi.ldap.connect.timeout=500
    ldap.connection.com.sun.jndi.ldap.read.timeout=15000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Settings for importing users and groups from LDAP to the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.enabled=false
    ldap.import.on.startup=false
    ldap.import.interval=10
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set either user or group for import method. If set to user, the portal will import all users and the groups associated with those users. If set to group, the portal import all groups and the users associated those groups. This value should be set based on how your LDAP server stores group membership information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.method=user
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.import.method=group
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the lock expiration time for LDAP import. By default, the expiration time is 1 day. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.lock.expiration.time=86400000
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>If set to true, the group filter will be applied, but only to groups in the specified base DN. If set to false, the filter will not be applied and all groups that are associated with the imported users will be imported regardless of the base DN. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.group.search.filter.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Specify whether group DN lookups will be cached during LDAP import and login. If set to true, this will speed up LDAP import and login, but updates to group attributes will not be recognized until the cache entry expires. The cache size and timeout may be configured in the configuration file specifed in the property "ehcache.single.vm.config.location". </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.group.cache.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if the portal should automatically create a role per group imported from LDAP. The role will be assigned to the group so that users can automatically inherit that role when they are assigned to the group. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.create.role.per.group=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set these values to be a portion of the error message returned by the appropriate directory server to allow the portal to recognize messages from the LDAP server. The default values will work for Fedora DS. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.error.password.age=age
    ldap.error.password.expired=expired
    ldap.error.password.history=history
    ldap.error.password.not.changeable=not allowed to change
    ldap.error.password.syntax=syntax
    ldap.error.password.trivial=trivial
    ldap.error.user.lockout=retry limit
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to use LDAP's password policy instead of the portal password policy. </p> 
  <p>If set to true, it is possbile that portal generated passwords will not match the LDAP policy. See the "passwords.regexptoolkit.*" properties for details on configuring RegExpToolkit in generating these passwords. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.password.policy.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to false when the LDAP user's password should not be imported to the Liferay user. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.user.password.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to autogenerate passwords for users imported from LDAP. </p> 
  <p>This property is only in use if the property "ldap.import.user.password.enabled" is set to false. </p> 
  <p>If an LDAP password policy is enabled (see the property "ldap.password.policy.enabled"), the password will be generated using RegExpToolkit. Set the "auth.pipeline.enable.liferay.check" property to false to disable password checking by the portal's internal authentication (which is not compatible with LDAP), and set the "auth.pipeline.pre" property to com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LDAPAuth so that password checking will be delegated to the LDAPAuth authenticator. </p> 
  <p>Note that enabling LDAP export, by setting the "ldap.export.enabled" property to true, may lead to overwriting the LDAP user's password with an autogenerated password. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.user.password.autogenerated=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set either screenName or plain text as the default password for the imported LDAP user. Setting the value to screenName will use the user's screen name as the password for the imported LDAP user. Setting the value to any other plain text value will use that value as the password for the imported LDAP user. </p> 
  <p>This property is only in use if the properties "ldap.import.user.password.enabled" and "ldap.import.user.password.autogenerated" are both set to false. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.import.user.password.default=test
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.import.user.password.default=screenName
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Settings for exporting users from the portal to LDAP. This allows a user to modify his first name, last name, etc. in the portal and have that change pushed to the LDAP server. This setting is not used unless the property "ldap.auth.enabled" is set to true. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.export.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if groups and their associations should be exported from the portal to LDAP. This setting is not used unless the property "ldap.auth.enabled" is set to true. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.export.group.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the values used to connect to a LDAP store. </p> 
  <p>The list of properties must end with a subsequent integer (0, 1, etc.) and it is assumed that the list has reached an end when the pattern or replacement is not set. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.base.provider.url.0=ldap://localhost:10389
    ldap.base.dn.0=dc=example,dc=com
    ldap.security.principal.0=uid=admin,ou=system
    ldap.security.credentials.0=secret
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Active Directory stores information about the user account as a series of bit fields in the UserAccountControl attribute. </p> 
  <p>If you want to prevent disabled accounts from logging into the portal you need to use a search filter similiar to the following: (&amp;(objectclass=person)(userprincipalname=@email_address@)(!(UserAccountControl:1.2.840.113556.1.4.803:=2))) </p> 
  <p>See the following links: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     http://support.microsoft.com/kb/305144/
     http://support.microsoft.com/?kbid=269181
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.auth.search.filter.0=(mail=@email_address@)
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>When importing and exporting users, the portal will use this mapping to connect LDAP user attributes and portal contact attributes. </p> 
  <p>See com.liferay.portal.model.ContactModel for a list of attributes. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.contact.mappings.0=aimSn=\nbirthday=\nfacebookSn=\nicqSn=\njabberSn=\njobTitle=\nmsnSn=\nmySpaceSn=\nskypeSn=\nsmsSn=\ntwitterSn=\nymSn=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>When importing and exporting users, the portal will use this mapping to connect LDAP user attributes and portal contact's custom attributes. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.contact.custom.mappings.0=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>When a user is exported to LDAP and the user does not exist, the user will be created with the following default object classes. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.user.default.object.classes.0=top,person,inetOrgPerson,organizationalPerson
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>When importing and exporting users, the portal will use this mapping to connect LDAP user attributes and portal user attributes. </p> 
  <p>See com.liferay.portal.model.UserModel for a list of attributes. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.user.mappings.0=emailAddress=mail\nfirstName=givenName\ngroup=groupMembership\njobTitle=title\nlastName=sn\npassword=userPassword\nscreenName=cn\nuuid=uuid\n
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>When importing and exporting users, the portal will use this mapping to connect LDAP user attributes and portal user's custom attributes. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.user.custom.mappings.0=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the user attributes that are controlled from the portal. When adding or updating a user from LDAP, these attributes will be skipped. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ldap.user.ignore.attributes=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.user.ignore.attributes=aimSn,comments,facebookId,facebookSn,greeting,icqSn,jabberSn,jobTitle,languageId,msnSn,mySpaceSn,openId,prefixId,reminderQueryAnswer,reminderQueryQuestion,skypeSn,smsSn,suffixId,timeZoneId,twitterSn,ymSn
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>When a group is exported to LDAP and the group does not exist, the group will be created with the following default object classes. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.group.default.object.classes.0=top,groupOfUniqueNames
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>When importing groups, the portal will use this mapping to connect LDAP group attributes and portal user group attributes. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.group.mappings.0=description=description\ngroupName=cn\nuser=uniqueMember
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Settings for importing users and groups from LDAP to the portal. These setttings are not used unless the property "ldap.import.enabled" is set to true. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.import.user.search.filter.0=(objectClass=inetOrgPerson)
    ldap.import.group.search.filter.0=(objectClass=groupOfUniqueNames)
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>New users and groups will be created at the specified DN. This will only be active if the property "ldap.auth.enabled" and "ldap.export.enabled" are set to true. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    ldap.users.dn.0=ou=users,dc=example,dc=com
    ldap.groups.dn.0=ou=groups,dc=example,dc=com
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr>

  <a name="CAS"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>CAS</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable CAS single sign on. NTLM will work only if LDAP authentication is also enabled and the authentication is made by screen name. If set to true, then the property "auto.login.hooks" must contain a reference to the class com.liferay.portal.security.auth.CASAutoLogin and the filter com.liferay.portal.servlet.filters.sso.cas.CASFilter must be referenced in web.xml. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    cas.auth.enabled=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>A user may be authenticated from CAS and not yet exist in the portal. Set this to true to automatically import users from LDAP if they do not exist in the portal. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    cas.import.from.ldap=false
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the default values for the required CAS URLs. Set either "cas.server.name" or "cas.service.url". Setting "cas.server.name" allows deep linking. See LEP-4423. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    cas.login.url=https://localhost:8443/cas-web/login
    cas.logout.url=https://localhost:8443/cas-web/logout
    cas.server.name=localhost:8080
    cas.server.url=https://localhost:8443/cas-web
    cas.service.url=
    cas.no.such.user.redirect.url=http://localhost:8080
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    cas.service.url=http://localhost:8080/c/portal/login
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to log out the user from CAS when the portal session expires. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    cas.logout.on.session.expiration=false
</pre>

  <a name="NTLM"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>NTLM</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable NTLM single sign on. NTLM will work only if LDAP authentication is also enabled and the authentication is made by screen name. If set to true, then the property "auto.login.hooks" must contain a reference to the class com.liferay.portal.security.auth.NtlmAutoLogin and the filter com.liferay.portal.servlet.filters.sso.ntlm.NtlmFilter must be referenced in web.xml. </p> 
  <p>Negotiate flags are set according to the the client's requested capabilities and the server's ServerCapabilities. </p> 
  <p>See the following link: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     http://msdn.microsoft.com/en-us/library/cc717152%28v=PROT.10%29.aspx
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    ntlm.auth.enabled=false
    ntlm.auth.domain.controller=127.0.0.1
    ntlm.auth.domain.controller.name=EXAMPLE
    ntlm.auth.domain=EXAMPLE
    ntlm.auth.negotiate.flags=0x600FFFFF
    ntlm.auth.service.account=LIFERAY$@EXAMPLE.COM
    ntlm.auth.service.password=test
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>See http://jcifs.samba.org/src/docs/ntlmhttpauth.html for more available properties. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    jcifs.netbios.cachePolicy=30
    jcifs.smb.client.soTimeout=35000
</pre>

  <hr> 
  <a name="Authentication Pipeline"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Authentication Pipeline</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class names that implement com.liferay.portal.security.auth.Authenticator. These classes will run before or after the portal authentication begins. </p> 
  <p>The Authenticator class defines the constant values that should be used as return codes from the classes implementing the interface. If authentication is successful, return SUCCESS; if the user exists but the passwords do not match, return FAILURE; and if the user does not exist on the system, return DNE. </p> 
  <p>In the pre-authentication pipeline, if you want to skip password checking by the internal portal authentication, the authenticator should return SKIP_LIFERAY_CHECK. This is needed if passwords are not imported to the portal. </p> 
  <p>Constants in Authenticator: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     public static final int DNE = 0;
     public static final int FAILURE = -1;
     public static final int SKIP_LIFERAY_CHECK = 2;
     public static final int SUCCESS = 1;
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <p>In case you have several classes in the authentication pipeline, all of them have to return SKIP_LIFERAY_CHECK or SUCCESS if you want the user to be able to login. If one of the authenticators returns DNE OR FAILURE, the login fails. </p> 
  <p>Under certain circumstances, you might want to keep the information in the portal database in sync with an external database or an LDAP server. This can easily be achieved by implementing a class via LDAPAuth that updates the information stored in the portal user database whenever a user signs in. </p> 
  <p>Each portal instance can be configured at run time to either authenticate based on user ids or email addresses. See the Admin portlet for more information. </p> 
  <p>Available authenticators are: </p> 
  <p></p>
  <pre>     com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LDAPAuth
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <p>See the LDAP properties to configure the behavior of the LDAPAuth class. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.pipeline.pre=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LDAPAuth
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    auth.pipeline.post=
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable password checking by the internal portal authentication. If set to false, you're essentially delegating password checking to the authenticators configured in "auth.pipeline.pre" and "auth.pipeline.post" settings. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.pipeline.enable.liferay.check=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited class names that implement com.liferay.portal.security.auth.AuthFailure. These classes will run when a user has a failed login or when a user has reached the maximum number of failed logins. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.failure=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LoginFailure
    auth.max.failures=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.LoginMaxFailures
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the following to true if users are allowed to have simultaneous logins from different sessions. This property is not used unless the property "live.users.enabled" is set to true. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.simultaneous.logins=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true if users are forwarded to the last visited path upon successful login. If set to false, users will be forwarded to their default layout page. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.forward.by.last.path=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>The login page reads a redirect by a parameter named "redirect". If this property is set to true, then users will be redirected to the given redirect path upon successful login. If the user does not have permission to view that page, then the rule set by the property "auth.forward.by.last.path" will apply. </p> 
  <p>You can set the redirect manually from another application, by appending the "redirect" parameter in a url that looks like this: /c/portal/login?redirect=%2Fgroup%2Femployees%2Fcalendar. This url will redirect the user to the path "/group/employees/calendar" upon successful login. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.forward.by.redirect=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Enter a list of comma delimited paths that can be considered part of the last visited path. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.forward.last.paths=/document_library/get_file
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Enter a URL that will be used to login portal users whenever needed. By default, the portal's login page is used. </p> 
  <em>Examples:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="examples">    auth.login.url=/web/guest/home
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to prompt a guest user to login when attempting to access a protected page resource in the portal. By setting this value to false, the portal will inform all users that a requested resource is not found if they have no entitlements to view the resource. The portal will not prompt for login even if the user was a guest user. This behavior complies with OWASP best practices. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.login.prompt.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Enter a friendly URL of a page that will be used to login portal users whenever the user is navigating a site and authentication is needed. By default, the portal's login page or the URL set in the property "auth.login.url" is used. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.login.site.url=/login
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Enter the name of the login portlet used in a page identified by the URL of the previous property (if one has been set). This will allow the portlet to have access to the redirect parameter and thus forward the user to the page where he was trying to access when necessary. You should leave the default value unless you have your own custom login portlet. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.login.portlet.name=58
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to disable any users from logging into the portal. Preventing users from logging into the portal provides a read-only version of the portal that can be used to minimize site outages during upgrades. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.login.disabled=false
    auth.login.disabled.path=/portal/login_disabled
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Enter a list of comma delimited paths that do not require authentication. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.public.paths=\
        /asset/get_categories,\
        \
        /blogs/find_entry,\
        /blogs/rss,\
        /blogs/trackback,\
        \
        /blogs_aggregator/rss,\
        \
        /bookmarks/find_entry,\
        /bookmarks/open_entry,\
        \
        /calendar/find_event,\
        \
        /document_library/find_file_entry,\
        /document_library/find_folder,\
        /document_library/get_file,\
        \
        /flags/edit_flag,\
        \
        /iframe/proxy,\
        \
        /image_gallery_display/find_folder,\
        /image_gallery_display/find_image,\
        \
        /journal/get_article,\
        /journal/get_articles,\
        /journal/get_latest_article_content,\
        /journal/get_structure,\
        /journal/get_template,\
        /journal/rss,\
        /journal/view_article_content,\
        /journal_articles/view_article_content,\
        \
        /layouts_admin/robots,\
        /layouts_admin/sitemap,\
        \
        /login/facebook_connect_oauth,\
        \
        /message_boards/find_category,\
        /message_boards/find_message,\
        /message_boards/find_thread,\
        /message_boards/get_message_attachment,\
        /message_boards/rss,\
        \
        /my_sites/view,\
        \
        /polls/view_chart,\
        \
        /portal/emoticons,\
        /portal/expire_session,\
        /portal/extend_session,\
        /portal/extend_session_confirm,\
        /portal/json_service,\
        /portal/license,\
        /portal/logout,\
        /portal/open_id_request,\
        /portal/open_id_response,\
        /portal/portlet_url,\
        /portal/session_click,\
        /portal/session_tree_js_click,\
        /portal/status,\
        \
        /search/open_search,\
        /search/open_search_description.xml,\
        \
        /shopping/notify,\
        \
        /wiki/find_page,\
        /wiki/get_page_attachment,\
        /wiki/rss
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <a name="Authentication Token"></a>
  <a href="portal.properties.html">Top of Page</a> 
  <h3>Authentication Token</h3> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set this to true to enable authentication token security checks. The checks can be disabled for specific actions via the property "auth.token.ignore.actions" or for specific portlets via the init parameter "check-auth-token" in portlet.xml. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.token.check.enabled=true
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the authentication token class. This class must implement com.liferay.portal.security.auth.AuthToken. This class is used to prevent CSRF attacks. See http://issues.liferay.com/browse/LPS-8399 for more information. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.token.impl=com.liferay.portal.security.auth.SessionAuthToken
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Input a list of comma delimited struts actions that will not be checked for an authentication token. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.token.ignore.actions=\
        /asset/rss,\
        \
        /asset_publisher/edit_article_discussion,\
        /asset_publisher/edit_entry_discussion,\
        /asset_publisher/edit_file_entry_discussion,\
        /asset_publisher/edit_page_discussion,\
        \
        /blogs/edit_entry,\
        /blogs/edit_entry_discussion,\
        /blogs/rss,\
        /blogs/trackback,\
        \
        /blogs_aggregator/edit_entry,\
        /blogs_aggregator/edit_entry_discussion,\
        /blogs_aggregator/rss,\
        \
        /calendar/edit_event_discussion,\
        \
        /document_library/edit_file_entry,\
        /document_library/edit_file_entry_discussion,\
        \
        /document_library_display/edit_file_entry,\
        /document_library_display/edit_file_entry_discussion,\
        \
        /journal/edit_article_discussion,\
        /journal/rss,\
        \
        /journal_content/edit_article_discussion,\
        \
        /image_gallery_display/edit_file_entry,\
        /image_gallery_display/edit_image,\
        \
        /login/create_account,\
        /login/login,\
        \
        /message_boards/edit_discussion,\
        /message_boards/edit_message,\
        /message_boards/rss,\
        \
        /my_sites/view,\
        \
        /page_comments/edit_page_discussion,\
        \
        /shopping/edit_order_discussion,\
        \
        /software_catalog/edit_product_entry_discussion,\
        \
        /wiki/edit_page,\
        /wiki/edit_page_attachment,\
        /wiki/edit_page_discussion,\

        /wiki/rss,\

        /wiki_admin/edit_page_attachment,\

        /wiki_display/edit_page_attachment,\
        /wiki_display/edit_page_discussion
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set a list of comma delimited portlet ids that will not be checked for an authentication token. </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.token.ignore.portlets=82
</pre>
  <p></p> 
  <hr> 
  <p>Set the shared secret that is used for requests where it is not possible to generate an authentication token (i.e. WSRP). </p> 
  <em>Defaults:</em> 
  <p></p>
  <pre class="defaults">    auth.token.shared.secret=BAHyWOT9TbPB
</pre>
